    <li> I am a male (cyclist) with course body hair, and this was my first time using an epilator, so my review will be base on the manufacture claims, against its performance, and targeting other first time Epilator users.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Claim: 72 Tweezer Heads for Fast, Long-Lasting Results&lt;br /&gt;Result: I was expected the one pass as promised, that did not happened, in fact I needed a few passes in some areas to achieve the desired results. Not so easy to keep engaging however.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The term \\&quot;gentle\\&quot; is used quite often in the product description, \\&quot;gentle\\&quot; is relative, based on your ability to cope with discomfort, I read the reviews and as such expected some pain/discomfort, from having my hair pulled from the roots. I believe I would have been better prepared mentally, if I the manufacturer did not use \\&quot;gentle\\&quot; so often. As a first time user, I hoped considering the discomfort associated, the process would be fast, and long lasting. For me it was not fast, it took an episode of \\&quot;Game of Thrones\\&quot; to completed both legs, this included discomfort breaks. It will get the job done, but not quite as claimed. I will post an update on how long the results last.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;UPDATE: I have reduced my rating from 4 to 3 stars.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After using the product, I could not see any hair left, but I could feel the stubble left behind. I believe this was the result of the hair that was broken by the device as opposed to being pulled from the roots. If your desired result is for smooth finish this will be a significant flaw. I wanted to hair removed and it was,, I did however, because of manufacture&#x27;s claim expect a more smoothend result (again take my hair type into consideration, maybe softer/thinner hair will break less..)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My hair growth was noticeable after five days. I had to epilate again after seven days. My \\&quot;Long Lasting Results\\&quot; is one week.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My hair was much less course when it regrew (compared to shaving)and epilating this time resulted in significantly less discomfort. There still is the stubble, and there was more irritation.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I still like the product, I wanted my hair removed and it was, just not as smoothly, gentle, and long lasting as the manufacturer&#x27;s claim.</li>
    <li> The Emjoi seems to just break off most of the hair.  It does pull out some,  I did let the hair grow out before I used it.  Have not had it very long and the hair has come back as soon as a few days.  Will continue to use and hope it does what it is advertised to do.</li>
    <li> Honestly, I am not super impressed with this.  I like the plug-in aspect, because it never loses power, and I like how powerful it is. It&#x27;s like plucking your eyebrows - it hurt the first few times, but you got used to it &amp; it stopped hurting. A couple of times the epilator caught a hunk of skin because it wasn&#x27;t stretched. It doesn&#x27;t hurt at all; it just scares you the first time.  Shaving under the arms is much easier than it seems it would be - again, make sure to keep the skin stretched. Also, I find the underarm hairs that grow back are much lighter, finer &amp; fewer.  The only problem I&#x27;ve experienced is hairs growing back just under the skin in a leg area; I can see them, but can&#x27;t reach them until they&#x27;ve finally grown through the upper layer. These areas are just on the outside of my calves, by my by knees &amp; I think it might be because I always wear pants &amp; sit all day &amp; that area is tighter against my legs. Several reviewers remarked about making sure when bathing to scrub the shaved areas well to exfoliate &amp; I don&#x27;t always remember to do that.  I bought the Emjoi about a year ago &amp; have been very happy with it. It has an electric cord that plugs into the bottom of the shaver &amp; reaches over 8 feet.  A nice option would be also rechargeable, but I definitely would choose electric above battery-only; you need to keep the constant power for shaving.  I&#x27;m surprised that no one (consumer companies/websites) has made an effort of comparing epilators by shaving one leg with one top brand &amp; the other with another top brand for easy comparison&#x27;s sake!  Regardless of whether you buy the Emjoi or the Braun, IT IS WORTH IT - especially for you ladies who have the embarrassing chin hairs!!  Jan 2013 update: I&#x27;m still using this great epilator &amp; loving it. My underarm hairs are so light and sparse that I can pretty much get away without saving for a month or more (between living in AZ &amp; my hot flashes, I always were sleeveless blouses). My chin hairs have also pretty much disappeared - I still shave every 3 or 4 days, but instead of hundreds of chin hairs, there are only about 5-10. The growth of hair on my legs is interesting - very few from the calf down, around my knees, and thighs, but somewhat more under and above the back of my knees, but still 1/3 of what was there before I started using the Emjoi. One thing: I shave my legs about once every two months, so if I had done it more often &amp; regularly, I&#x27;m sure the hair would be much sparser. It&#x27;s pretty much painless to use everywhere, except the pubic area, which I think is because the hairs are so much thicker than everywhere else. I can still highly recommend this!  April2017 Update Sometime after my last update in 2013 the tweezers head on the first Emjoi started catching, i.e. stopped turning, at first it was every once in a while, then more often, until I just couldn&#x27;t use it any more. Luckily, I had bought a warranty with Square Trade and got a full refund, which I used to buy a new Emjoi.  After three or so years, the electric cord/adapter for the 2nd Emjoi stopped working. I didn&#x27;t have the one from the first Emjoi anymore and my Square Trade warranty had expired, but I found another that fit at one of the big box stores.  The issue Iâve been experiencing the last month or so is that epilator seems to be shaving instead of epilating. I started noticing that the hair is growing back much faster and thereâs a lot more of it on my chin. Also, up until the last month or so, when the hair on my legs grew back, it was always soft and I could barely feel it, but now I feel the stubbles, like I used to get from shaving. So, this leaves me with two options: 1) buy another Emjoi AP-18, or 2) some other epilator brand. Once again, I have spent many hours reading hundreds of reviews, and based on the reviews, have (once again) narrowed it down to the same Emjoi, or one of the Braun models.  End result: I&#x27;ll buy another Emjoi AP-18 because I don&#x27;t want to be stuck with hair on my legs, face, under arms, or bikini area due to a dead/empty battery. Since the hair on my legs and underarms has become so sparse (before I started epilating 10 yrs ago, it was very heavy &amp; dark), I usually only use the Emjoi once every 4 â 6 wks, but it takes me a good hour at least. The Brauns are only good for about 40 minutes. Also, several reviewers complained about the battery completely dying within 6 months to a year. My own experience with most things with a built-in battery is that they start slowing down as the battery drains and eventually completely die (cell phones, Bluetooth, tablets, tooth brush, electric razor, handheld vacuum, etc.) which is why I buy cameras that use lithium batteries and buy spare batteries. Even though Iâve had to replace two units after 2.5 and 4 years, I still feel that the Emjoi works great and is worth the $80 (which has not gone up in price since the first one I bought 10 yrs ago)!   And, again, I can still highly recommend this!</li>

    <li> This is the first epilator i&#x27;ve ever owned, having shaved all my life, it being the easiest and least painful option for hair removal. i did a lot of research online before deciding on an epilator, and even more before deciding to try this one. i have a very low pain tolerance, so i was quite sceptical, but willing to give it a go given that i&#x27;d read in a number of places that epilators are now nowhere near as painful as they used to be, and i had read many reviews stating that this one was around the least painful there was.    i have just received my new epilator and used it for the first time, and i can definitely say that it is really not that bad at all. Yes, there is a very mild pinching sensation as each hair is removed, but its definitely well within my ability to tolerate it, and even do an entire leg at a time. It is far easier to see whether the you&#x27;ve been successful with  removing the hair with an epilator, and with this one, you do need to go over the same spot a few times sometimes, but mostly, it does a great job first time round. i doubt there&#x27;s a hair removal technique yet invented that really never needs to go over the same area twice.    Like with all hair removal, you will need to do it regularly at least to start, because your hair grows in cycles, and when you do it today, you&#x27;re not catching the hairs that are still growing in the pores and haven&#x27;t peeped out as yet.    One cannot complain about fast regrowth or ingrowns in relation to epilators, because that&#x27;s really individual to each person&#x27;s body, so the factors i believe are important are:    * Is it painful? - Not enough to worry about. Also, i could actually feel a sharp, pricking sensation in a number of the pores for a while afterwards, but nothing disturbing.    * How fast can you get it done? - For me, this epilator was perhaps a couple of minutes faster than shaving, but nothing to write home about.    * How smooth are you afterwards? - Very smooth, very smooth.    * Is it easy? -As easy as shaving with this one.    * Can i attack multiple parts of my body with the same tool? - Yes - the same head can do the upper lip, underarms, legs and bikini area. However, the instructions say that when using on the upper lip, one should only target individual hairs at a time, and use only one of the heads.    * Can i use it wet and dry? This one is dry only, but i don&#x27;t see that as a problem.    * Is it easy to use? - Very. It sits easily in your hand, and while the instructions state which way round you&#x27;re supposed to hold it, the shape of the body makes you want to hold it that way anyway. The on/off/ slider is easy to intuit, and really, its much like shaving from there, except that you&#x27;re supposed to pull your skin taut as you go. Easy peasy.    * Is it easy to clean? - Yes. It comes with a little brush that is easy to hold and easy to use on the epilator head. The head is detachable for easier cleaning if you wish, and comes off as a completely separate unit, with no internal working exposed on either the body or the head when it is removed. All you need to do is brush off the hairs and you&#x27;re done.    * How noisy is it? - Moderately, but quieter than many electric razors. Its not quiet, per se, but it didn&#x27;t scare my cats when i turned it on next to them.    * Can i go out looking fab straight away? - i would say no. This is a small drawback i guess, to epilators in general, not just this one. i have quite white skin, and it was decidedly marked with little red dots for a while afterwards.    * Is it worth the money? - Admittedly i should probably answer this question after at least a couple of months usage, but so far, i&#x27;d say yes, and based on the majority of the reviews i&#x27;ve read (many of which are after a significant period of use), i would say yes.</li>

    <li> As far as epilators go, this is a great product. It&#x27;s stronger then the battery operated ones I&#x27;ve used, and with the extra tweezing capability it gets the job done faster. Of course it hurts a bit at first use, as some reviewers have mentioned, but tweezing hair will most likely hurt,especially in sensitive areas. The trick to using it and making it less painful, is making sure you take a hot bath or shower prior, and pulling the skin as tight as you can in the area your using the epilator. The tighter the skin, the better contact it has with the hair your trying to remove, and the less it pulls at the skin, which often creates some of the pain. You can also tilt it so only one of the heads is contacting the skin until you get used to using it. In areas where the hair is thicker, you may have to make several passes to get all the hair. Once you use this, if you continue to do maintenance on the tweezed area before all the hair grows back out, it won&#x27;t hurt as bad as the initial use. It also has a nice safety feature that prevents you from pressing the heads down to hard upon your skin, which is a great added feature. I had only minor skin irritation in the area that was tweezed, and it lasted only briefly, so do it a few hours before your planning on exposing the area. I also find moisturizing after tweezing helps diminish this problem. I think it is especially nice in the bikini line areas, where razor bumps are often a problem, there was no redness except for the initial one mentioned before, which is gone very quickly. I went on a camping trip for a week and could stay in shorts with no razor stubble growth, that&#x27;s a bonus!</li>

It sounds simple enough to hold it as instructed my Emjoi, but there is a technique to it, and you naturally get better the more you use it. I have started moving it in all different directions (left/right, up/down, circles) in short motions and it works great. I have been doing my lower legs every few days for almost a month and my last epilation was by far the best! I feel like I got ALL except for the extremely smallest of hairs this time. Keep in mind that hair grows in cycles. So when you have hair 2 days after you epilate, it&#x27;s not the same hair growing back. It&#x27;s DIFFERENT hair, that wasn&#x27;t there when you epilated.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;When I first used it on my legs, I was not satisfied at all and questioned my purchase. The first swipe is the worst. If it&#x27;s your first time epilating, I would recommend \\&quot;tapping\\&quot; that area with the epilator instead of \\&quot;sweeping\\&quot; it in a smooth motion. After you have tapped an area about 3-5 times, the \\&quot;sweep\\&quot; is infinitely more tolerable.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2.) After epilating, I use a cotton ball + witch hazel and then apply a triple antibiotic ointment. This prevents infection and red bumps. To prevent ingrown hairs, I exfoliate daily in the shower using some rough gloves. After I get out, I use the towel to rub away any dead skin. If I see any ingrown hairs, I sometimes use a pumice stone. UPDATE: Be careful about this! Early on, I was exfoliating too harshly and it left my skin looking red and bumpy. Be sure to give your skin a break to heal. It will look and feel a lot smoother. To moisturize, I use olive oil - no fancy fragrances/ingredients that can cause irritation to the inflamed skin.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;3.) Give it time. Don&#x27;t expect to do all of your body in one day. Do small areas at a time. Don&#x27;t try to be 100% thorough the first time. Just do a little bit each day.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;P.S. A.) It is extremely loud. B.) The cord doesn&#x27;t bother me at all.</li>

It was incredibly painful and would leave red marks/tiny scratches on my skin. I have never had this problem with the Emojoi (thank goodness!).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cord vs Cordless:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I may be different from others, but my favorite thing about the Emojoi is that it is corded. Why? No internal battery to deal with! The Braun worked great at first but after a few months the battery would die in about 15-20 minutes - which did not work if it took an hour to do my legs. What&#x27;s worse, it would take two hours to charge. So that is over three hours dedicated to epilating and trust me, it got old fast. I hated epilating, it became such a chore I just shaved most the time. Dealing with a cord (which is conveniently very long) is way better than worrying about a dwindling battery life and a two hour charge time.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One downside is the Emojoi corded unit cannot be used in the bath or shower. I rarely used my Braun in the shower. I did not find it any less painful or more effective, and it was just easier for me to epilate outside of the bath. The normal cap worked just fine for my legs and armpits, though I never used the epilator on my face.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Emojoi only came with the cord and a cleaning brush, but considering I never once used the other attachments provided from Braun, Emojoi wins this catagory as well - less is sometimes more.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Comfort:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Emojoi claims to be &#x27;gentle&#x27; and if you&#x27;ve ever epilated, you know there is nothing gentle or comfortable about ripping your hair out at the root. This is a great feature that the Emojoi lacks. It might seem silly, but you&#x27;d be surprised how helpful it is!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall, compared to the Braun, the Emojoi AP-18 wins.     <li> I was excited, though nervous, to try the Emjoi Emagine (AP-18 Dual Opposed 72 Tweezer Head Epliator) because the hair on my legs grows fairly quickly, meaning that the results of shaving don&#x27;t last very long.  As a reference, I shave every other day and don&#x27;t wear anything that will expose my legs on the off day because my hair is already noticeable.  So, after reading reviews, I purchased this epilator.  Not knowing how long the hairs had to be (ok, .4mm, but seriously, who can measure that?), I waited for over 48 hours before trying it the first time.  I then, due to very limited success, tried again the next day (greater than 72 hours at that point).  Below are my thoughts on various categories:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Pain: This is what was most concerning to me.  I have to say, this is the one area where I was pleasantly surprised.  Do you feel it?  Yes.  Is it unbearable, even the first time?  No, not to me.  Sometimes I&#x27;d be targeting a specific hair (more on that later) and, after a pass, be thinking that it hadn&#x27;t worked because I didn&#x27;t feel anything, only to be surprised that it was gone.  Sometimes, though, I specifically could feel that I had gotten it.  The sensation is a little like a light electric zap, not really like a pinch.  After using it, my legs felt tingly for about an hour.  Not really painful, just noticeable and unusual.  As a side note, I did use it on my underarms and that was more painful and I&#x27;m not sure I actually got any hair.  To be fair, the hair there was much shorter, having been shaved the day before, but I suspect I was mostly experiencing skin pinching not hair removal.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Ability to remove hair: Not so good.  I tried many different approaches - with the growth (as the guide says), against the growth.  Long passes, short passes.  Quick passes, slow passes.  No pressure, light pressure.  The thing that seemed to work best was light pressure, slow, short passes.  Direction seemed hair dependent - sometimes I&#x27;d have no success for several passes going in the growth direction, then I&#x27;d go against the growth and get it the first time.  Other times it&#x27;d be the exact opposite.  After about 15 minutes I began targeting the hairs I could see, specifically.  Contorting my leg in various ways to get the light to hit it just right to see a patch of hair, then going over and over and over it.  Eventually, in the end, I don&#x27;t think there was a single targeted hair that I ever gave up on, but some took several (i.e. more than 10) passes.  For hair I couldn&#x27;t see (light in color or very fine) I didn&#x27;t stand a chance.  I gave up after about 30 minutes and went and shaved my legs.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Look of legs after use: Not so good.  The epilator, on both uses, left red bumps on my legs, similar to the kind you get with razor burn or heat rash.  These bumps were everywhere I had pulled hair from which, though not a lot, was still not a pleasant sight.  The bumps seem to go away in about half a day, but I would not have been able to wear shorts either day after use without the bumps being highly visible.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall: I&#x27;m returning it.  I could see how this might be useful to minimize the amount of shaving you&#x27;d have to do on a vacation, but it wouldn&#x27;t eliminate it.  You&#x27;d still have to shave at the same interval, there&#x27;d just be less hair to remove.  I would say this certainly wasn&#x27;t worth the time, pain, or effort.  I was prepared to be in pain to look good and save shaving time, but in the end I got less pain than expected, but also fewer results.  This is the first epilator I&#x27;ve ever used, so I can&#x27;t say that this is a bad product when compared to others, but compared to expectations, this falls way short.veral passes going in the growth direction, then I&#x27;d go against the growth and get it the first time.     <li> I have used several kinds of epilators, home wax kits, gotten professionally waxed etc for over 20 years.  I had used the Braun for several years and loved it, but like many other users, was frustrated with how long it took to epilate my legs.  I have exceptionally hairy legs with very dark course hair and it would take a total of 4 hours to clear my legs of hair with the Braun, if they were super hairy.  Like others have mentioned, the braun clears every single hair, whereas the emjoi, clears ALMOST every hair. (I think it might be because the emojoi breaks a few hairs off instead of pulling them.)  If you want that perfectly shaved feel, you would have to spend hours with the braun.  For me, I can use the emjoi in about 1/4 the time, and the time savings is definitely worth the few tiny hairs that remain.  I will also mention here that because your hair grows at different rates, the first time you clear your legs, whether it be with waxing or epilating, because all of the hairs have grown out, your legs will be much more smooth, and remain smooth for a longer period than subsequent epilations.  Therefore, just like with shaving, you have to deal with needing to re-epilate in a few days if you want that perfect smooth surface.  Personally, I can live with not being 100% hair free, so I epilate about once a week.  That is the best system for me.  If I let it go two weeks or more, then epilating becomes much more uncomfortable as you are pulling out so many hairs.  Plus it takes so much longer.  If you really want smooth legs, and you could afford it, I would suggest buying botht he emjoi and the braun.  I would clear the majority of hairs with the fast emjoi and then go over it again with the braun.  I haven&#x27;t done this personally, as I mentioned, I will tolerate less than smooth legs.  I do have a few additional suggestions for those of you who haven&#x27;t used an epilator before.  I had waxed for years, using both professional waxers and a home waxing kit.  But because of a terrible experience with the old &amp;#34;epilady&amp;#34; of the 1990&#x27;s I was literally terrified to try to epilate.  I finally broke down and bought a braun after my south american neighbor told me how much better it was than the epilady.  But I was still scared, and it sat in my closet for months after purchasing it. Finally, I did it, and it really was nothing as bad as the old epilady, but that could have been due to the fact that I had been waxing all those years.  If you have never epilated before, I STRONGLY suggest getting just breaking down and paying a one time cost of getting waxed by a professional just once before you start to epilate.  If you do that, then just a few hairs will grow back at first, and you can epilate them out without the torture of tearing ALL of them out at once.  I have done it both ways many times.  Especially when I had the braun, I as a working mom, I just wouldn&#x27;t have 4 hours to devote to it, so my leg hairs would grow and grow and grow. Even for me, after all those years of waxing, epilating ALL the hairs at once is really terrible.  So my biggest advice is keep up with it and you will love it.  For me, this is much easier to do with the faster emjoi.  No matter which brand you buy, if you do it at least once a week, it will go fairly easily.  I epilate everything with the emjoi, legs, arms, tummy, mustache, underarms, and a pretty close (but not crazy) bikini line.  And it takes me a total of only about 30-40 minutes with the emjoi if I do it once a week.  It would take longer if let the hair grow.  I can&#x27;t imagine how long the braun would take to do all of that.  It took 4 hours just to do the legs, but again, I often had let it go so long that my legs were really hairy.  I LOVED the emjoi at first.  It was SOOOOO much faster than the braun.  But the problem is, that it stops working after a while.  This is in fact the second emjoi I have bought.  And I will probably buy another one somewhat begrudgingly.  I loved the braun too, but it just took too long.  I will also mention that I am prone to ingrown hairs.  One thing that has really helped me is to use a loofah both before and after epilating.  I also try and do a quick loofah every time I am in the shower.  Your legs will never be as smooth as shaving with epilating.  (But they will actually be smother than waxing which may surprise you.  The epilators get many more of the tiny hairs than waxing does and fewer of them break.)  I could never go back to shaving at this point.  My hairs are so course that they are almost sharp when shaved.  But with either epilating or waxing, the hair is obviously pulled out completely, so when they do grow back, the end is a fine tip that isn&#x27;t nearly as irritating.  In the end, I do recommend both the emjoi and the braun, as well as the Clean and Easy home waxing kit.  Which is the one I used for years and was mostly happy with.  If you are going to home wax, it is by far the best.  For me, the time savings of the emjoi justifies me having to purchase a new one every year or so.</li>

    <li> I waited to write this review after I had used this product a few times.  My review compares this product to the original Epilady coil epilator (made in Israel) and to the Braun Silk-Epil model 5318.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;First some general comments:&lt;br /&gt;1. Pain - all epilation is painful. As a woman from the Indian subcontinent, I have lots of coarse hair and hair removal is something I&#x27;ve lived with for most of my life. I first started sugar-waxing at home in the 1970&#x27;s - very messy process. But because I&#x27;ve been yanking hair out from its roots for a long time, it doesn&#x27;t hurt much anymore, especially on my legs. That said, underarms are quite painful the first time you do them. So once you start, don&#x27;t stop! Because if you let the hair grow out, it will hurt like the dickens again. Also, I can&#x27;t do my bikini area at all.  Too much pain! I use pre-waxed strips instead. Some people mention epilating after a shower. I guess this helps. I always epilate after I shower so that my skin is free of all lotion and deodorant, so I can&#x27;t really compare.&lt;br /&gt;2. Ingrown Hair - yes this is an issue. For some reason it&#x27;s a bigger problem for me with waxing and epilating than shaving. My solution is to use a loofah in the shower, very frequently. Dry brushing your skin with a mitt also helps. Those puffy plastic mesh things don&#x27;t work at all, too smooth. Most of my ingrown hair occurs where my legs rub together since I usually sit with my legs crossed.&lt;br /&gt;3. Time and repetition - epilation takes more time than shaving and you do need to go over the area more than once to remove all the hair. But I can wait a week or two between treatments vs shaving which I&#x27;d have to do pretty much every day so it&#x27;s worth it. In terms of frequency, I use the epilators on my underarms and calves once a week and on my thighs and forearms once every two weeks.&lt;br /&gt;4. Corded vs. Cordless - I had both corded and rechargeable coil Epiladies (original and &amp;#34;Ultra&amp;#34;). I found that once the battery on the rechargeable unit wore out, it seemed to slow down even when it was plugged in. So now I only use corded units.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Original coil Epilady - I started using these about 20 years ago. I found them very forgiving in terms of how they had to be held against the skin, and how fast or slow you had to move them around on your skin. You could move it in straight lines or circles. They worked very well and they seemed to remove more hair in one pass than the newer designs. But I actually thought they worked better on longer hair than shorter hair. And their head shape meant that I never could do my underarms.  But they lasted a long time - about 15 years! Obviously they were pretty well built.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Braun Silk-Epil 5318 - After my Epilady bit the dust, I moved to this product. This older model&#x27;s tweezers have two metal teeth vs one plastic and one metal. I have seen other reviews that mention that two metal teeth are better than one being plastic. That said, this product works very well for me. You need to follow its directions, though. Move slowly in long swoops and hold the device at a 90 degree angle against your skin. I use the slower speed on the device because I thought the faster speed was causing more hair breakage. Also, I work against the growth pattern of the hair. This device is the best for getting into nooks and crannies and works well in the underarm area, because its head is fairly small and its a bit curved. It works best with hair around 1/4 to 1/2 inch long, and seems to get even the finest hair out.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;When I was using the old Epilady I had to shave my underarms. But I decided to try epilating them with the Braun and it is fantastic. The large number of tweezers makes it about 30% faster than the Braun. Also, the dual opposed head means you can go in various directions and it still works great. It&#x27;s tweezers also have two metal teeth, by the way. You still have to follow the directions. Hold the device at a 90 degree angle (upright) against your skin. Move in small swipes. I use the slower speed. The device works well on shorter hair, just like the Braun.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Now the bad - why I give it four stars instead of five. It is loud! Louder than the Braun. But the more important issue is that it&#x27;s head is quite large, and flat. So it is harder to use in the underarm and behind-the-knee areas.
